RATING: 5
Reveal a card, then read about the check. Determine how to modify the check, then roll the die. Reveal the next card, look at the next check, roll the dice. Reveal card, roll the dice. Reveal card, roll. Reveal, roll. Reveal, roll...

Sorry, but there just isn't enough meat to it for me that I'd consider this a great game, this is just a string of dice roll after dice roll after dice roll. See, it's very repetitive. You can't come up with some imaginative ways of problem solving like in real role play, and instead are limited to overcoming the odds of the roll again and again by just a standard dice roll. I'm not that impressed by it.

RATING: 7
Interesting take on the dungeon crawl genre. It's a deck builder but one that happens in slow motion between quests.  It's basic in gameplay and the main mechanic is pushing your luck to go faster and deeper through the location decks.  It could get samey if Paizo don't publish more interesting adventures than find and kill the villain.  Overall enjoyed by the group I play it with and each quest doesn't take too long (45 minutes to an hour with 5 players) so several can completed in a session


I'm not sure about how re-playable it is but if you have a group that buy in to the loot, kill and level up serial game play it supplies it's worth a look.  Suspect we will play the campaign and enjoy the journey but it will then sit on the shelf.

RATING: 8
Wow what a pleasant surprise! It has the deck building ideals akin to Mage Knight - but a much reduced instruction set for play. It has a huge amount of variety (even surpassing Mage Knight) in cards and situations. Each character feels very unique. The scenarios are simply stacks of self-contained cards - but its sufficient to carry a slight story along if you're willing to read the flavor text. For me, it's my newest dungeon crawler. More variety than anything I've seen before and much faster. It represents much of the mechanical interest of an RPG, but with more structure, more smarts. Really like it.

All of these factors make it a game I'll play on occasion (at least often enough to play through the mission packs), but it's not something I would want to play every week or invest in myself.  As far as highly-expandable cooperative games with a fantasy setting go, nothing beats the Lord of the Rings Living Card Game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An excellent card-based game that seeks to replicate RPGs.  It does so rather well, capturing many RPG flavors by its mechanics.  It does tend to boil down to dice rolling with a smidge of problem solving, but I like how it feels and works.  Sometimes I can see my cleric hefting her warhammer and wildly swinging at a gnoll to no avail.  Other times I want to weigh my dice and figure out why they hate me so.

So I love this one, even (particularly?) as a solo game.  Why not a higher rating?

(1) Very repetitious.  To me, the primary replay value is in the different character classes and that's kinda crummy.

(2) Character progression is slow.  It seems like they modeled it on RPGs, where progress and development is measured in sessions and development is *very* incremental.  This does not jibe well with the punchiness of most modern board games and you can feel the disconnect in Pathfinder.  Your character will get better, but it will take time and many adventures.

Those being said, I like this one a lot and I don't regret my purchase one bit.  I'm very glad I picked it up and I eagerly await the next adventure pack!

[update]
So got around to playing through the base game and the first expansion adventure set, and still not sure where to rate this, so I will still pass on that.

The game has a ton of luck in it, but it does not take that long to play, so not a huge deal, right?

Well, maybe it is the biggest deal ever.  So we were playing and in the second to last adventure I own, my friend's character dies.  We are sure the rules are just go and replay that adventure and move on.  NOPE, rules say that character is irrevocably DEAD.  Start a new fresh level 1 character.  This is the dumbest thing I have seen in a long time.  It is a coop game so we ignored that, played the adventure again and finished it up.  But now I feel like playing more would be cheating.  So I am probably done with this game.

RATING: 8.25
Incredibly fun game. SOOO much future potential. It's a game changer.

However, there are some quality and production issues as it stands right now.

Some cards have a slightly off-colored back (more green) than others cards from both the base and character add-on sets. This makes them more apparent while playing, some moreso than others. These mostly seem to come from the Burnt Offerings adventure pack (#1) included with the base set, though occasional cards in the base set also are a little off as well. It's not terribly bad (at least in mine), but it can be noticeable while playing.

Other factors in the design, appearance and text of the cards is a little amateurish compared to similar products (e.g., Warhammer Invasion, Android Netrunner, Magic the Gathering), and it's odd that conventions that are pretty much staples to card games weren't adopted in the presentation and format of cards in this one.

Finally, the rulebook is okay. Not great, but it does the trick with only some ambiguity. Could've been better presented, I feel.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I like my dungeon crawlers fast playing and simple.  Pathfinder certainly has a low rules overhead.  With up to four players it moves along reasonably quickly, without much down time.  I've played once with five and then it did seem to drag. 

Pathfinder feels closer to a role-playing game than some dungeon crawlers I prefer. There are the polyhedral dice, the division of spoils at the end of an adventure, the clear differences between character classes, and a real sense of a character progression.  Perhaps the closeness to an RPG reminds me too much of the element that's missing - the role playing.

In addition to that, there was nothing at all memorable about the three adventures I have played so far.  Not the locations, nor the monsters, nor the big bad have made much impression.  I contrast that with Dungeoneer, where each deck has its own distinctive flavour.

In addition to that, while I like the deck building element better in Pathfinder than in Mage Knight, it still feels a very un-thematic mechanic.  Let me see, I have used my mace once to hit a monster, so I won't see it again this adventure.  What?  

Production quality is good.  The artwork could have done more to evoke those senses of wonder, threat or terror.

RATING: 9
Brilliant adventure card game with a good storyline.  You work through over 30 scenarios (split across the base game and 5 add-on decks) battling many different foes and gaining cards to upgrade your character decks as you progress.

I'm loving this game.  It plays fairly quick and I've been enjoying playing through a scenario to relax when I get home from work.

Some of the scenarios are more challenging than others depending on what characters you have chosen to play with.  There are some great synergies to be found with different combinations of characters and the game plays very well solo with a team of two.  This gives good replayability in playing through the game a few times with different combinations (more if you get the additional character pack)

RATING: 5
Has the same problem as many co-op games, where 
1. The most experienced player can just tell everyone else what to do to win.
and
2. There's usually a "best" thing to do, and once you figure out how to play there's not much of a game left since there are few tough decisions.

In fact you can basically just copy and paste my Zombicide review here.

Supposedly future adventure packs will make the game more varied and interesting, but I didn't really enjoy myself enough playing the base game to want to give them more money.


Also important to note is that this basically just simulates the fighting portion of a tabletop RPG (my least favorite part) and has very little actual role playing (my favorite part). Your own opinions of those two aspects of tabletop gaming will likely greatly determine how much you enjoy Pathfinder.

RATING: 8.75
PROS:
-Can be played solo or up to 4 players (6 with the Character Add On expansion) scaling well in difficulty (actually it gets more difficult the more players you add - hint for whoever consider this an "easy" game)
-Unique and satisfactory combination of deck building, deck managing, and dungeon-crawling RPG-like experience
-Innovative way of playing cards: some are just revealed to generate an effect, others are displayed in front of you for the turn, others put back in the deck, others get discarded, or combinations of those effects. Simple and elegant without unnecessary complexity
-Brilliant characters with different mechanics each, but all of them viable, fun to play, and balanced. Smartly captures the approximate mechanics/feeling of each class from the RPG game
-Character progression works really well, you will feel attached to your character and the threat of perma-death will add nicely to the tension (I rather loss a scenario than see my rogue die!)
-Many decisions to take, strategy is important (especially on how you build your character and your party)
-Great artwork
-Expandable and very replayable
-Rules are not actually complicated. Easy to learn
-The base box has room for every card in all expansions (note: except if you sleeve them...)
-Developers are very responsive and participative, gathering feedback from the community and implementing changes accordingly
-Official online PDF version of the character sheets available if you do not want to write on your cards

CONS:
-Luck can affect some games: as you are always time-limited to 30 turns, if you happen to draw all the big baddies first, that particular scenario will be much easier to complete (this is partially mitigated by the fact you are playing a whole campaign of 30+ scenarios).
-For die-hard RPG players some mechanics will be painful to swallow (why is the party throwing away all the items they do not want to use instead of storing them in a nice chest for future adventures? :D)
-The manual needed to be corrected to clarify many rules and mechanics - free online PDF file available
-Many cards needed to be officially FAQ'ed. Although few errata are noticeable at first and none is game-breaking, once you realize so many cards needed corrections you start to wonder if the unusual card you just encounter is phrased correctly and you feel the urge to check the official FAQ again just to be sure (which can be distracting)
-More than one dice set should have been included. Almost every turn you roll more than one die of a specific type, as a lot of the card effects are something like "add one extra die of the same type to this roll"
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.9
I was hesitant to check this out for some time, but ultimately relented since I have friends that might enjoy it. A faithful translation of the original Pathfinder RPG Adventure Path into a card game of exploring, and close enough in that it still uses dice mechanics, skills/feats, just in a way pertaining to advancing the scenarios and characters. You get plenty in the base box for a few adventures, and the insert comes with space for the Add-On packs and additional packs in that Adventure Path. Plays smoothly and the fact it has a solo option makes it fairly attractive for those nights you can't get an RPG session together.

RATING: 7
2/1/15: Merisiel is my favorite character so far.  Does well on her own and her dexterity with ranged weapons makes her pretty good.  

The change in colors on the card backs between editions is very noticeable.  Unfortunately this requires sleeving the cards with opaque backs, I'm not going to bother doing that, but it's something that I notice every time I shuffle and deal cards.

1/15/15: We'll see how well it holds up to repeated playings, and whether or not every playing starts to feel the same, which is hard to avoid without a DM.  To me it's light years beyond Thunderstone.  It does a very good job of encompassing a D&D 3.5 (Pathfinder) adventure in a card game.  The adventures allow you to accumulate equipment and experience, advancing your character.

For me it fulfills it does a good job of fulfilling the dungeon crawl game much better than some other alternatives.  I was never attracted to Castles of Ravenloft because they were too simple and too abstracted.

Rating would be 1 higher if there weren't erata.  Hopefully the next printing will clear up some rules questions and card errors.

6 is the maximum number of people, and while I'll recommend it with 6, there is noticeable downtime between turns.  Our first adventures took about 90 minutes each with 6 players.

Includes the Burnt Offerings Adventure Deck - (#1)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Pretty good little co-op game. I think this wins for me because it is less of a co-op, and more of an RPG, with cards instead of character sheets - and it works. I love that there's "perma death" and it seems like the different characters have different feels to them.

Now, that said, it's a _LITTLE_ bit on the solitaire side of things, but that might not necessarily be a bad thing. I could see actually picking this game up just for that reason. It's fun in the times where your team mates have to jump in to help you out, but it seems like that's very rare - and there's quite a bit of downtime between turns.

I like the art in this game - quite a bit. So that's a big positive for it. It looks like they just ripped images from my old D&D 3rd edition book. 

I do have two complaints - well, one, and a minor nitpick. First, the nitpick: I think this game doesn't need the different sized dice, and it really slows the game down. I feel like you could either eliminate dice entirely from the game with another "fate deck" that your character has to build up personally, (or that your whole party could maintain and draw from... which would make it less solitaire-like) or just do it with multiples of D6. ... screw that, I want the fate deck. That sounds really cool.

Second, my actual complaint is that a lot of the cards feel very same-y. The enemies are generally just "roll over this, and you don't take damage." I want to WIN things from the enemies. I want to sell my old equipment and gold, and be able to purchase new cards in between missions... 

So my overall take is: the game is good, but it doesn't quite go far enough.

RATING: 7
Előrebocsátom, hogy sosem szerepjátékoztam, így semmi viszonyítási alapom nincsen. Nem tudom, hogy a Pathfinder szerepjátéknak mennyire tipikus és mennyire jó, én társasjátékosként (és társasjátékként) tudom csak értékelni. Lehet, hogy ami nekem új, az egy szerepjátékosnak evidens, de ez van:)...

Először is adódik a kérdés, hogy miért vettem meg? Nagyon szerettem volna egy ilyesmi hangulatú játékot, amit lehet szólóban is játszani. Kipróbáltam, hogy mennyire működik, de egyelőre csak a legkönnyebb küldetésen vagyok túl. Ennyi alapján nehéz véleményezni, hiszen ha végig akarok menni minden küldetésen, tisztán 1 hétig játszhatnám, ez még csak amolyan bevezető volt. Mégis van pár dolog, ami máris kiderült.

Az első, ami már a kibontáskor is látszott, hogy nagyon igényes a játék. A doboz szép, tágas, a kártyák grafikája pedig sokkal közelebb áll hozzám, mint mondjuk a Sentinel of Multivers-beli rajzok. Egy kicsit csalódás volt, hogy nincs tábla, de végül is nincs rá szükség. Tulajdonképpen a játék "csak" egy nagy rakás kártya. A sok angol szöveg ellenére sem vészes a nyelvfüggőség, a különböző típusú próbák köré van felfűzve a legtöbb kártya szövege.
A doboz kialakítás nagyon professzionális, még a kiegek dobozainak is van hely, úgy van kialakítva, hogy 6 kieg elférjen mindenestől. A baj csak az, hogy kártyavédővel nem kalkuláltak. Bugyistól max 2 kiegnek van hely. Ezt leszámítva nagyon tetszik ez a fajta tárolás (fajtánként külön fakkban a kártyák), de szükség is van rá a játék mechanikája miatt. A kiegek vásárlására nem csak az ösztönöz, hogy előre meg van a helyük a dobozban, hanem az alapkoncepció is, ami azért kicsit szemtelenség, de őket is meg lehet érteni:) Ha valaki csak egy küldetést csinálna meg, megteheti, van az alap pakliban is néhány. Ha valaki komplett kalandot akar (Meghatározott küldetések sorozata), annak sincs akadálya, de ha valaki a teljes Pathfinder kalandsorozatot végig akarja csinálni, akkor szép sorban meg kell vennie a kiegeket, amiknek a terep amúgy is elő van készítve:) Lenyúlás felsőfokon. De legalább igényesen csinálják.
Egy kicsit a játék működéséről: a játékmotor tetszik, különböző helyszíneken próbáljuk elkapni a gonosz(oka)t, lezárni előle(lük) a helyszíneket, megpróbálhatunk összedolgozni ha többen vagyunk egy helyen, találhatunk tárgyakat, stb. Valaki azt mondta, neki az nem tetszik benne, hogy nem adja vissza a kalandozás érzést, hanem csak kockamenedzselés. Ez egy kicsit tényleg így van, minden lap amit meg akarunk szerezni, vagy amit le kell győznünk, különféle próbák elé állít minket, amiknek a fő eleme a szereplőnk személyére szabott kockadobás, bár ezt kártyákkal módosíthatjuk.  És ha már a szereplőknél tartunk: nagyon jól ki van dolgozva a karakter-fejlődés! Külön lapon célszerű vezetni (netről letölthető, ha nem akarja valaki a gyárit firkálni), hogy karakterünk melyik képessége épp milyen szinten áll, a próbák során milyen kockamódosítókat kap, mennyi a kézlimitje, hány tárgya, fegyvere, stb. lehet a pakliban, stb. A karakter fejlődéséhez küldetéseket kell teljesíteni, kb. egy küldetés tekinthető egy játéknak, ha társasjátékos aggyal közelítem meg:) Küldetés végén a karakterünk pakliját aktualizálni kell, és ha nem akarjuk rögtön folytatni, el lehet tenni egyben a paklit(külön erre a célra is vannak fakkok:)), vagy akár helyére is lehet tenni minden kártyát, a lapon is nyilván lehet tartani, hogy miből áll a paklink, és melyik küldetésnél tartottunk, bármikor rekonstruálható az állás. Ha több küldetéssorozaton is átrágjuk magunkat, és karakterünk elér egy bizonyos fejlettségi szintre, akkor el kell döntenünk, hogy milyen irányba fejlődjön: 2 féle út közül választhatunk, ezek lényegesen eltérőek, a döntésünktől függően teljesen más jellegű képességeket fejleszthetünk a későbbiek során.
A küldetésekhez több helyszín van rendelve, minden helyszínnek külön paklija van. A gonoszok pontos helye meglepi:) Így lehet hogy végigkutatunk egy helyszínt, elmegy vele a fél játék, de nincs ott akit keresünk. A játék legnagyobb erőssége szerintem a nagyon sokféle lap! Persze lehet azon vitatkozni, hogy mennyire ad ez valódi változatosságot, de nekem az egy próbajáték alapján úgy tűnt, végtelenek a lehetőségek. A szabály megengedi saját küldetések, saját karakterek kitalálását. A sokféle helyszín mindegyike más-más keret-lehetőségeket ad, rengeteg féle gonosz, szövetséges, tárgy, fegyver stb. van már az alap pakliban is.

Mivel a karakterem épp csak beleszagolt ebbe a világba, és még semmit se fejlődött, annyit mondhatok csak, hogy az első benyomás nagyon jó, de nem tudom eldönteni, hogy elég jó-e a játék ahhoz, hogy beszippantson:) Adok rá egy biztató pontszámot, tekintettel arra, hogy ebben a kategóriában nem ismerek mást.
Jó lenne kipróbálni gyakorlott szerepjátékossal is, de az úgy már más jellegű (esetleg egész napos) időráfordítást jelentene. Így hogy egyedül játszom, simán mehet egy küldetés lefekvés előtt:) A játék egy hibája talán, hogy az előkészület kicsit hosszú, de szerintem bele lehet jönni.
Először féltem, hogy nehéz lesz nyilvántartani a sok dolgot a karakteremmel kapcsolatban, de annyira lassúnak ígérkezik a fejlődés, hogy ezzel nem lesz gond.
Még egy dolog: ikonrendszer, kártyán lévő jelölések, stb. nagyon egyértelműek, korrektek.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
I couldn't resist buying the overhyped card game of the year. And I am quite glad I bought it...

The gameplay in Pathfinder is very streamlined: you go (or stay) to a location, flip the first card of the location deck and roll dice (to acquire it if it's a boon, to defeat/avoid it if it's a bane).

The things that distinguish the game are two:
1. Your character is a deck of cards, and it is permanently modified after each scenario, with the loot you find during the adventures.
2. The gameplay is very thematic, with the descriptions on the cards, and the whole adventure path / adventure / scenario tree contributing to a very enjoyable experience.

The overall comment is: the game is very light and luck-driven, but is also quite fun and compelling. It's not a game for everyone, but it's a game my s.o. and me will gladly enjoy for lighter non-thinky nights!

RATING: 8
I love what Pathfinder ACG is trying to do; getting an RPG experience from a card game is a dream come true for many gamers. It's a tall order -- and no, this is not equivalent to a tabletop RPG -- but it is a really fun game that allows you to make checks rolling dice, progress your character through a story arc, and customize their growth over time. [b]Rise of the Runelords[/b] is the place to start if you're interested in this system, offering a pure RPG fantasy theme and the most straight-forward ruleset amongst the various versions. If you like the game, it's very easy to create your own experience by mixing and matching characters, locations, enemies and items of your choosing, even grabbing from the other versions and numerous expansions. Lots of fun with great replayability; this one's a keeper!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Just purchased this game. It's a very different sort of game -- a card game that is also an RPG (role-playing game). Both Andrea and I enjoy it a great deal!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Without the emotional investment in the characters and their development, the game seems repetitive and one dimensional. The game's mechanisms are simple to grasp and playtime doesn't seem too long.

RATING: 5
After playing base set and pack 1: A masterpiece. Very entertaining and addicting. This will be the first game where I think about developing my character without playing.

A fantastic game design. Simply an amazing game and my best purchase 2013...yet. The rules are well written but they had released an updated version where they gave more detailed descriptions.

Cannot wait to play the next scenarios.

Nonetheless: It takes too long since new adventures come out...


EDIT after finishing pack 2 and starting pack 3: Rating down to 7. (I do not do that that often...)

The game becomes grindy. The card packs are not that exciting. Not that many strong enemies, not that great rewards. So the game becomas a duty and you hope to get one of the few better cards. It is not a game system problem, but the card packs have to be better.

EDIT 2: The rating is dropping further. When cards do not offer more the whole lack of game design becomes obvious. There is nothing going on in this game. No decisions, no real cooperation and it all about flipping cards. That would be OK if the cards would be cool. But the packs are very, very boring.

I lost almost any will to play it again.

The basic idea after all is good but the card design is not. This is where the game lacks...and it is a card game.

RATING: 4
The main game consists of playing the odds, which is no bad thing in itself, just quite repetitive.

For me the theme didn't really come through because the locations are populated with a randomiser. This means that you can find a demon, a wild animal and member of the thief-brotherhood at the very same barn – a very mixed and inconsistent group :(

But the main drawback for me is the multiple cards that all tweak the rules a bit (the scenario card, the location card, the character abilities). It's not that easy to get into it and get a steady flow of gameplay. Too often I had to check and re-read the same cards and on occasion even search for a bit of information I knew I read somewhere but just couldn't find right now...

With multiple plays it may become easier and thus better, but it's not my game so I'm not sure I will really get familiar with it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
My 1st big turkey. I loved this game when it came out, and ranked it among my top 3. Now it's just "meh", here are the reasons why.

1) Early on, it's great to find and acquire new and very useful cards. By the 4th expansion, there was almost nothing good to find. Marginal improvements at best. The game stopped scaling, except for the difficulty of checks.

2) The theme is mild at best, and there is no meaty storytelling in between quests. So it turned into "flip a card, and see how high you need to roll"

3) It seemed like they were trying to hard to come up with new and different checks, and many of the newer banes checks were a bit too obscure.

4) The news that the characters were done after the 6th expansion, took the wind out of my sales for building them up for a new adventure.

5) I lost excitement waiting for new expansions to be released. Not a specific complaint to this game, but I saw no need to play a campaign twice. So it was 5 and done for 2 months.

6) I played some dungeon crawlish games(Descent, M&M, & Claustrophobia) which made me realize that this game was missing too much theme, story, and depth for me.

7) After 1-6, the game stopped being fun, and became frustrating & monotonous.

RATING: 6.9
The game is one of the most addictive games in my collection.  I play the game solo only.  I play two different characters through the missions.  It really is fun, but it will be necessary to keep on buying expansions to keep the game fun. I purchased two expansions so far, and I may stop there.  It is a money sucker like no other, and that does not work for me.  I have put some money into expansions for Lord of the Rings: the Card Game and Android Netrunner, but it is not absolutely necessary to keep on dumping money into these games to keep them fun.  With the expansions I have for these two games, I can stop at any time and have a game that I will play for many years to come.  With Pathfinder, the card game, the expansions are necessary to keep the game alive.  This is a negative point for me.  

In my opinion, the game hits hard at first, and then becomes less and less fun to play.  This one has a shelf life for me.

RATING: 5
For me the best way to describe this game is, Talisman: The Co-op game.  I don't think there is anything inherently wrong with PACG.  It does seem to generate plenty of conflicting reviews.  It's not an RPG and the people that are expecting it to be are the ones who end up the most disappointed.  Or at least it seems that way.  The game does generate plenty of stories if you let it...however if you need little FFG-esque flavor texts and story blurbs on every card then you're going to be upset.  The game is about letting the players tell the story.  It merely sets up the skeletal framework of an adventure.  The rest is up to you and your friends.  Overall, this is an excellent co-op card game with lots of replay value.  People with zero imagination should avoid.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
2013, fully co-operative, experience game; essentially an RPG without the RP. Very repetitive game with some character level-up but only if you play a campaign game (i.e., multiple plays). Not much variation or cool stuff to find, just an extra +1 to die rolls for "awesome" items. The worst thing is replayability which is pretty low. It is just too samey except for all of the die rolls, and it's an infuriating search for the bad guy before the time clock (30 card blessing deck runs out). In the end, the campaign game and level-up (Risk-Legacy style) can be fun/interesting/addictive, but it's just a crafty way of getting you to spend money on expansion packs (due out every 2 months or so). Bottom line: AVOID unless you want to play campaign and burn cash on expansions.  StormKnight's 9/27/2013 review summarizes the game (and flaws) nicely.

Others say: too easy (win ~90% of time) with 4p or less, but gets harder if you buy the expansion to go to 6p.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

This was the cat's whiskers a year ago for me but after a whirlwind romance it has gone upstairs out of the regular play area with the last two packs to play intact. Hopefully it'll get some rainy day plays but I think its best days are over for me.

RATING: 8
Having a blast with this one - two player, one character each, the monk and the barbarian. Hurts to see all those spells go by, we'll probably play it again all the way through but going with a magic user next time :)

Lots to like here - progression, but not over the top, each scenario is a little different, but similar enough that we don't need to keep digging into the rules.

And again another 2 player this time Sorcerer and Ranger - and now it hurts a bit to see all the weapons and armor slide on by ;) 

Heartily recommend if you're looking for an adventure cardgame with that dungeon crawl rpg feel.

Why not a '10'? Well some elements are a bit weak or missing - no puzzle solving or other non-combat stuff you might see in an RPG, here it's all beat the monster, avoid the monster, beat the trap, avoid the trap. But saying that still bags of fun :)

Helps having the extra flavour text though.

Update - now have the iPad app, traded the physical game!

RATING: 6
10x10 2014. Not an RPG or even an RPG replacement really.  Vasel mentioned Talisman in his review and I think that's actually a good reference point for how this game feels.  It's an adventuring type game where you flip over cards to see what you encounter.  The main mechanic is kind of a slow deck building over multiple sessions.  And the persistence of your character over multiple sessions is really cool.  I like that it's co-op but you're also working for your own character's benefit, getting loot to improve your deck and increasing stats is perhaps the most satisfying part of the game.  The different types of dice are fun to roll too and give that old school D&D vibe.  If you get all the expansions there is a ton of game- over 30 scenarios.  I do think after playing it a lot the theme kind of disappears and it becomes a little mechanical.  So in the end, I had some fun with this but playing it a bunch gave me enough of the experience.  I don't think I would want to play through it again or get subsequent sets.

RATING: 7.5
My most-played game (in terms of number of plays) since I started logging plays in 2004. 

One of the solutions to the roleplaying game conundrum (which is, briefly, how to get the pencil and paper roleplaying experience without the need for a consistent group and a dungeon master).  This game gives you linked scenarios, character advancement, and rolling for success.  

On the negative side, since it is a boardgame, it has a ruleset that specifies what you can do (rather than being open-ended like a true RPG). And since it is a boardgame, roleplaying is not required -- in fact, you can play it with roleplaying but it slows the game down. At times, the game appears to be somewhat repetitive (explore, try to roll high enough to succeed at a check), which I hope will push me toward doing more on the roleplaying side of things. 

On the positive side, it's a game that my wife and stepson will both play, which makes it a pretty rare thing. And the different characters play differently, which is nice -- more replayability. 

Currently playing this every 2 or 3 months at a monthly game night. Hope to eventually get through all of the scenarios in Rise of the Runelords, but I realize that will take quite a while at this rate. 

Suggestions:
1. The first time someone plays, it may be a good idea to have him/her play with an advisor to help with the game's vocabulary and options. 
2. It's easy to forget that you have special abilities. It's a good idea to look at your character's special abilities between turns to remind yourself of what you can do that is unusual. Making the most of your special abilities is necessary in order to beat the game on a consistent basis. 
3. I suspect the game is best with 3 or 4 characters, especially if you are playing with new players. With 5 or 6 characters, you really have to pay close attention to what you can do when it is not your turn. With 1 or 2 characters, your decks and special abilities won't have much variety and it may be hard to succeed at some of the checks. 
4. I don't think this is a game that can be won on a consistent basis if you take your turn and then leave the table and come back when it is your turn again. (Some of my fellow players have done this.) Looking for ways to cooperate even when it is not your turn will make it easier to win.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
I held off on trying this for years because I thought it looked so stupid: flip a card, roll dice. Flip, roll. Rinse and repeat. 

When I finally came around to trying it, however, I found myself unable to stop playing. There is something compellingly, compulsively fun about this game. The theme really comes through, the cards combo in interesting ways, and you really have to be cooperative, solving problems together and helping each other out wherever possible. And the leveling-up mechanism is perfectly timed: upgrades happen slowly, but not too slowly, so that you want to keep playing to see your character grow.

I'm over 80 plays in, and still loving every minute of this game. Skull and Shackles is great, too!

RATING: 4
Most of the game is flip a card, roll some dice, hope that you roll high. Sometimes you will have to ask yourself how many resources you want to burn in order to feel like the odds are good enough in the rolling high part. Now, I am not a fan of post-decision randomness, the only game I felt did this well was Arcadia Quest, so mechanically, this isn't the kind of game I'm going to enjoy playing.

The between missions levelling up could be really cool (it certainly is in Arcadia Quest), but the cards simply aren't interesting. There's no combos to build and most of the decisions boil down to would I rather have the sword? Or the sword +1? Which isn't actually a decision at all.

Essentially, this feels like a card game version of grinding in CRPGs. In terms of the gameplay, where you just draw card after card, trying to play through all the cards so as to be able to close locations and end the scenario. Also in the levelling up, where you have to play through scenarios in order to get slightly better at things you could already do before (and I'm willing to bet that the monsters get tougher the further you go, so improving is illusionary).
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
There's actually some really neat stuff at work here. There's a lot of randomness, and to get good at the game you really have to learn how to account for it and control it. Mostly through the use of Blessings, but also in generally how you build your deck.

This is a game of risk analysis and you are constantly being asked to make choices. That's great, but I feel like a lot of the plays feel fairly obvious after just a game or two. So while I enjoy the game, I feel like there's something missing in the turn-to-turn play for me.

So what you have more or less, then, is a game largely about its progression system. Yeah, most RPG-ish games have character progression, but it's a fun and different way to do it and ends up being fairly addictive.

It's fascinating how each class feels true to its RPG roots through use of the card mechanics. Since magic users tend to have bigger hand limits, they're capable of taking more damage per turn and thus feel more vulnerable.

A weird compliment, but the box insert in this is fantastic. It makes setup and teardown a breeze and even has handy-dandy slots for future adventure packs and your current party. Nice!

It does feel a bit odd to have put the "first" adventure pack in its own cardboard box WITHIN the box... but I guess it's nice if you dig consistency. Also I'm not sure if it's just my copy, but the backings for the cards in the first adventure pack run slightly darker so you can tell the difference between the base cards and the "expansion." Not a huge deal, but it does feel like a pretty n00b mistake.

Update: Ended up trading this. At its best this game is a 7, but the scripted turn-to-turn play really hurts it after awhile. Yeah, occasionally you get some tense choices with the Blessing system but unfortunately those become less and less frequent the further into the campaign you go. The difficulty just plateaus after a point and never picks back up. It really is a shame. I even bought the next Adventure pack and didn't even have to play it to know it wouldn't fix this. The enemy stats are roughly in line with everything in the base game and don't even scale based on adventure number, which is both surprising and a HUGE disappointment. I can happily live without this game.

RATING: 8
If you like RPGs, especially the fantasy genre, and enjoy card games/deck building this is a must. There is a lot of luck involved, but the players have control over that luck by choosing what cards they want to have in their deck.

It feels about the right difficulty but has a bit of a learning curve. It is challenging especially with new characters and it often feels that failure is just around the corner, but I've found that the win ratio is high enough to keep stop it becoming frustrating.

This is ideally a game that is played over many sessions, improving the character each time.

-edit-
After having the game for several months I've lowering the score I've awarded the game from 9 to 8. For a game than needs to be played long term, there isn't enough variety in the gameplay.

RATING: 3.5
Holy sh*t this game is overhyped! It’s probably the most overhyped game I can think of. Of course this is just my opinion, and I respect that a lot of people love it, and its rating cannot be questioned, but it’s just not for me. At all. I don’t see the appeal in this game. Yes, on paper I thought it sounded great that you get a character you can evolve over many plays etc., but in reality the game itself is so extremely repetitive and boring… I mean, you do the same thing over and over again: turn over a card and roll the dice to do a skill check. Sometimes you fail, other times you lose, but rarely is the penalty for losing too serious as we’ve never lost a game (always won rather easily), and I know that it’s the general consensus that it’s just way too easy. 

Come on, the whole idea of cooperative games is that they should be hard as hell so you often lose so that you want to go back and win! This desire is non-existing for me in the case of Pathfinder. Even the way you kill the monsters and his henchmen is the same. Yes, there are various bosses and locations and weapons etc., but the chore gameplay mechanism is extremely boring because of its repetitive nature. I don’t even feel like there is a story behind the game. Yuck. Sorry, this game is simply bad, and I do think it will drop in the ratings as people (perhaps?) start to feel it’s just “more of the same”.

RATING: 5
An RPG themed game that simply doesn't hold up to repeated play.

Like an RPG, the game succeeds at making you care for the characters in your party.  That party doesn't really cooperate as they would in an RPG however.  In fact, their lack of cooperation can be very counter-intuitive. 

After playing a set of characters through the skinsaw adventures I traded my set away.

Perhaps our characters got lucky early on, several chests were opened and good weapons found in the Peril's mini adventure.  For whatever reason, we found almost nothing of value to acquire during the Burnt AP, and only had two of the adventures require a second try to complete.  Similar story in Skinsaw, with the exception of the tough Foul Misgivings scenario where Ieasha's unbeatable whammy kiss almost killed several characters. 

The game quickly becomes repetitive because ... it _is_ incredibly, criminally repetitive.  And not just at its core, its repetitive right on the surface.  If you're not discovering goodies and encountering interesting monsters/banes ... that repetitiveness quickly grates.  As an example, there are sites that require encountering a Bandit henchman every turn ... a criteria we simply ignore as by this point our character can dispatch such puny scum with impunity, so why waste our precious time rolling for it?

The game has many production flaws, to the point of being amateurish.  The rule book leaves an inordinate amount of questions (as witnessed by the 75+ pages of forum posts) in part because it has several illogical stipulations (such as characters in the same location can't (for most purposes) fight together)).  Card backs from the base set have a different hue than those of adventure packs an unforgivable error in a game of this sort as it means AP cards are obvious in a stack.  And there is practically no attempt at providing a back story or narrative structure to tie scenarios together (but there's an excellent adventure guide here on BGG).

I tried he first expansion AP (Skinsaw) which failed miserably to win me over to the concept of spending $20 for more of same repetition.  The game has some merit, but the production gaffs and repetitious gameplay keep it from being a real winner.

In the end, there are simply too many other good games to play, several in this genres, although none seem to allow decks built across numerous game sessions as Pathfinder does.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Not a big fan of deck building games but the folks at paizo have made one here which works rather well. 

With a bit more complexity, this is what the Lord of the Rings LCG wanted to be. It is capabale of providing a good balanced, fun game whether solo or up to 6 players. 

My only grumbles are the cost of the base game (paying for air), and that there isn't enough variety in the cards that you get. Some cards are auto no-brainers to keep, while others give bonuses to rolls that currently don't exist in the game, making them worthless.

I think paizo have a good game on their hands here, providing that they keep it going as a single game and not make whole new box sets based on different RPG adventure paths. Keep everything compatible and things will be fine.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
This could very well be one of the most disappointing games I've ever played. I love RPG's. I love having a character with stats. I love rolling dice for skill checks. 

I don't like this game.

I'm not criticizing it as just "flip a card and roll a die". I'm criticizing it because of the plentiful opportunities for choices the game could have had and just didn't bother to flush out. For example:

-Though it's more thematic to not know what card you're encountering until you arrive at a location, without knowing what the differences are in the cards beforehand, the locations lack a strong identity against which a decision can be made. Instead, one is just making a decision based on the location's special "effect" which often doesn't relate to what's going on in a given turn. This makes choosing a location several degrees less interesting than it could have been. 

-There are too many instances where the math just doesn't line up for a character. Though it's possible another character might be able to help, it's not a guarantee. This creates "nothing" turns where a player just can't do anything. This unfortunately reminds me of games like Mille Bornes where you're essentially "blocked" until you just so happen to draw or acquire the right card. 

-All of the special effects on the locations plus the special effects of the scenario theoretically seem like they should produce a thematic feel. Instead, they reinforce to me the idea that "less is more". Take a game like Pandemic. A player has a special ability unique to them and they might have a card or two with a special ability. The choice surrounding these is when to use them and how to use them (which is good). However, you don't see every space on the Pandemic map have a special ability because that would be more distracting than helpful in setting up meaningful choices for the players. One spends more time in the Pathfinder card game trying to keep track of things rather than making decisions about those things.

-The set-up time is disproportionate to the quality of game one is being offered. I personally don't feel like the lengths the game designer went to to create thematic reinforcement for the different locations pays off. Having no spells in the deck at one location and lots for another doesn't make me feel like I'm exploring a particularly magical area. 

All in all, this game is unfortunately less than the sum of it's parts. Each of the ideas in the game, in isolation, seem good but there's just no real pay off in them (at least not for me).

I've tried house ruling the game into something I would consider "playable" but I'm now to the point where I'm having to make drastic changes to really see any improvement and I've still got a long way to go. 

All of this is not to say that enjoying the game is some sort of indictment on a person's gaming tastes. I'm also not saying that this game has to be anything more than a relatively straight forward card game in order to be fun. It doesn't have to be an RPG. It just has to be a game that's fun to play and it's just not that for me - and I truly wish it was otherwise. 

Update: Eventually sold this.

RATING: 8
I've played the first scenario three times now in order to teach myself the game.  The first two attempts went rather too well and gave the impression that the game is too easy.

I thought the third run through with the cleric and fighter combination would be a walk over.  The game bit back, the random monsters were tough,  I failed to close out the first location after discovering the first henchman, subsequent henchmen took a long time to locate and finally the cleric's weapon cards and most of the blessing cards were initially unavailable.  I started to make low rolls in combat and consequently needed to spend a lot of the clerics actions up on self healing.

I had one turn left for the fighter and one location left open and the only way I could win was a confrontation with the villain.  I explored uncovering the villain won the combat and kept my perfect record so far with no time to spare.  The best laid plans do not survive contact with the cards and dice but it does add to the drama.  

I believe this kind of game needs uncertain outcomes and random elements for replay.  

Upside:
Scenario Replayability
Drama
Character Progression
Card Driven Narrative

Downside:
Ultimate Success Can be Down to Dice and Card Draw
Mechanically Repetitive (scenario variation will be key to long term appeal)
Rules are Difficuly to Reference
Game Design Assumes Consequent Purchases (but there is quite a lot of game play in the base set)
Game Balance and Character Variation May Suffer if Players are into Min-Maxing

I will be re-reading the rules in the light of the first three games and this game lends its self to learning as you play.  I have used the least generous interpretation when in doubt and I do not expect to have given myself too many advantages by getting rules wrong.

Three characters seems to a sweet spot for difficulty.  Played this game twice with two friends and the game was won on the last turn of the card in both cases.  Could go up to 9 if the new scenarios have sufficient variation.  This could turn out to be a money pit over next two years if Piazo have ways of extending the games appeal.

2015 Looking forward to this on IOS.

RATING: 5
I had high hopes for Pathfinder ACG as I wanted a long-term game with an element of noticeable progression, but sadly this one just doesn't deliver. 

The biggest problem with this game is that there are WAY too many random factors that essentially dictate whether or not you'll be successful: from the composition of the location decks, to the quality of the cards you add to your own deck, to the binary success/failure outcomes of actions tied to dice rolls, to good ol' fashioned luck of the draw, when you win in this game it feels more like it was because the stars aligned in your favor rather than you and your teammates devising a winning strategy. 

This could be forgiven if a game weaves a compelling narrative, but there is essentially none. Each scenario has a paragraph or so of narrative context given to it, but there isn't much to differentiate one scenario from another once you start actually playing the game. You're just drawing a bunch of cards, then rolling a bunch of dice hoping you get lucky enough to find and beat the villain-of-the-day before you run out of turns, and if you win you move onto the next one. It's a very dry and mechanical experience, which isn't something one would expect from a game that tries to present itself as an RPG-lite. 

For all my criticisms, Patherfinder ACG is at least an honest attempt to blend RPG and board game, and it isn't entirely without merit. The game, while dull, does mostly work, and the character building aspect is nothing if not detailed. However for the amount of time and money this game demands as an investment (it's clearly purpose-built to sell expansions), it's a rather poor value overall. If you want an RPG, just play an RPG.

RATING: 6
Very conflicted feelings about this game... I really enjoy having your character become better and better as the game progresses, and it can get quite addicting. Also, I was disappointed with the design of the cards. Don't get me wrong, I really like Paizo's artwork (look at the Pathfinder RPG rule books, a lot of the art seems to be pulled from there), but the way it was used in the cards themselves it doesn't give it justice and is rather bland to look at.

I may give it a few more tries, but I am glad I didn't buy it before playing it.

RATING: 9
Picked this up in November of 2013 based on the reviews and play-throughs available on BGG.  I explained the game to Jen before I picked it up at a FLGS and promised her that she could get her own custom-colored dice to play the game.  We started with Harsk (me) and Merisel (Jen) to learn the game and it went very well.  I've tried playing this solo with just one character, but didn't have very much success.  We finally played this as a foursome with Valeros, Lini, Merisiel and Seoni ... the game was quite memorable with a win in the first scenario on the second to last turn of the game.

We're now playing with two parties of four, the second of which has just finished Trouble in Sandpoint.  The second party includes Ezren, Harsk, Lini and Kyra.  In hindsight, I think another damage dealer or maybe Lem would have been a better choice for Lini since we have two characters that are being used for cures when Kyra could probably handle it all on her own.  We've had Lini drop one of her cures, which makes her a little more fragile, but with more options for spells.

RATING: 4
I think I wanted to like this more than I actually like it.  It is by no means even close to replacing a tabletop rpg for me.  The theme is there, but the flavor doesn't really come through.  Yes, when I play I read the flavor text, and try to create a narrative that explains the events as they unfold, but it is still lacking.  At this point I've played all of the scenarios through 4.5 of the chapters, and there are only two that really stand out in my mind (one is a zombie apocalypse, and the other involves a dam bursting and flooding a town).  All of the others have just been playing whack-a-mole with the villain.  

Why have I played so much if I don't like it that much?  A good buddy of mine enjoys playing it, and I enjoy playing it with him.  The two of us have stuck by our characters as they have slowly evolved over the course of the "story."  I can't think of any other board/card games that do that.  It is the one thing that the PACG does well, and is fairly unique in that regard.  I highly doubt I'll be picking up future iterations.

Edit:  Chris Deavellar's thoughts, which are much more eloquent than mine, sum up how I feel, so I have taken the liberty of reproducing them here: 


For me, there's two shades of disappointment with this game. Firstly, I find the game as it exists to be...dull. Not awful, just boring. The mechanics, decisions, and cooperative gameplay all leave me wanting. Secondly, I find that I punish this game for what it isn't. That's never entirely fair, but playing this game leaves with this frustrated sense of what it could have been.

Criticizing what it is is, of course, subjective. Many have said that there's more to the game than "flip a card, roll a die", but to me, that's what the game feels like. Sure, we get to decide which deck to flip cards from. We get to play cards to give us more or less dice, and even solicit dice from other players via blessings. We get do play cards to flip another card, if we're feeling frosty. But at the end of the day, I find the act of picking a deck, flipping a card, and rolling a die to be thin. Worse is that the act of fighting a monster is the exact same as the act of finding a useless potion is the exact same as fighting a Henchman is the exact same as fighting the villain.

The persistent character deck seems so tantalizing, but you can't really morph your character into anything beyond what it is. I've played two characters thus far (Monk and Sorcerer). I hated the Monk. His deck/hand management actually seemed to work against itself, and I felt no sense of my deck clicking. The Sorceress works much better. But, even with her deck functioning better, I find that she plays the same way. She has a bunch of cards that add dice. She doesn't feel markedly different from the Monk. The deck setup just seems to function better. 99% of the loot you find during a session is useless. The majority of it is just variations on what you already have, rather than improvements. This never makes my character feel any sense of progression, and makes looting feel superfluous. The game is so overloaded with stats and dice, most of which do nothing. There are massive amounts of keywords, and roll types, and items, and everything just feels the same.

The game seems to actually discourage cooperation. With only a couple of exceptions, being in the same locations is generally useless at best, and harmful at worst. The theme just totally breaks down for me in this respect. The idea that the Ranger can shoot an arrow into the air from the Church to help me out in whatever underground dungeon I'm in, but if he were standing next to me he could do nothing, along with basically every other character except for the fighter. The only thing to do on someone else's turn is drop a blessing to help out, generally at the cost of being effective on your own turn (more a problem with the Monk than the Sorceress, but still). When I play the aforementioned Pandemic, or Gears of War, or Arkham Horror, we're constantly talking about what we're doing and where we're going. With PACG, I find myself waiting for my turn, or waiting for a blessing solicitation. I don't feel like part of a team of adventurers trying to locate and stop the villain. I feel like I'm trying to flip and burn as many cards as fast as possible to find the card that I'm looking for.

What I wanted was a cooperative dungeon crawl in card form. A game where my party traverses dangerous dungeons fighting our way to defeat some nefarious evil, collecting fat loots along our way. I wanted a character with character. I wanted loot that made me immediately want to slay something larger and tougher. I wanted monsters that didn't act like potions. I wanted a villain with personality, with a climactic boss-fight, perhaps even with a little AI that required teamwork, and a little puzzle-solving. Sadly, what I got, was flip a card-roll a die. Hell, even though we read the scenarios aloud, I couldn't tell what the hell is going on, and frankly the game hasn't given me any reason to care.

To sum up...I'm mostly punishing this for what it isn't. This is all subjective. The game just bores me, and obviously isn't for me. But damn, it seems like it should be. It seems like the elements are there for a GREAT game. It seems tantalizingly close to something I would love. But it just isn't, and that sense of lurking greatness makes it all the more disappointing.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Players are RPG heroes, cooperating to defeat a scenario, which forms part of an ongoing campaign.  Characters can level up after a scenario.

Weird game, pitched as an RPG card game.  Players take on a character (I was a dwarf ranger named Harsk), and build a deck of items, allies, weapons, etc.  That deck represents your health and if it depletes, you are dead.  The deck can be "recharged" by placing cards underneath, to keep your health topped up.

The game involves characters moving to locations (individually sculpted decks, based on setup rules - i.e. the woods are full of monsters, the academy full of spells), flip a card, and interact with it in some way.  This may involve fighting it, attempting to acquire it, etc.  Acquiring a card increases your deck potential, making you stronger.  

The goal of the scenario changes (I assume), but in ours we had to locate a villain, defeat it, but ensure every other location was "closed down" so he couldn't run away.  After literally 75 minutes to play five turns and understand the rules, we quickly defeated the scenario.

I can't say this game is great - I'm astonished at the love and BGG rating.  It simply involved flipping a card and rolling some dice, augmenting the roll with some equipment from your hand - it was hardly a challenge.  There was really no thematic connection here - this is not a role playing game.  As a solo game it may be mildly diverting, but as a cooperative game for four adults, there are much, much, much better options out there.  I will play it again to see it improves, but it only has one more chance...

RATING: 7
On its surface, it is mainly just flip a card, roll some dice.  However, there are some interesting decisions to be made, and teamwork between characters is key.  I find it strangely compelling in a way that Descent 2 was not for me.  Perhaps there is some merit in stripping the idea down to its essence.  I think the idea of slowing developing my character is the hook for me.  Whether that is enough to keep me interested through 6 adventure decks remains to be seen.

UPDATE Oct 2014:
We're about halfway through adventure 1, and the shine is starting to come off this a bit.  We'll see how far we get.  I think that the most interesting thing about this game is the way you build your character, and while that is fairly novel for this type of game, I am not sure I ultimately find that compelling enough to sustain my enthusiasm.  

UPDATE Nov 2014:
Well, my son (age 7) gave me a very well reasoned agruement as to why Pathfinder was not his favorite game.  "I have to wait 10 minutes between my turns, and when it is my turn I barely know what I'm doing."  Fair enough.  As for me, I am finding the game repetitive, and gaining a +1 here and there is no longer thrilling me.  I am also perplexed as to how I continue to find this game so finicky to deal with rules-wise.  
I think I'll be turning to Lord of the Rings Card Game for a similar questing card game, but with more interesting mechanisms.  I'm also looking forward to Assault on Doomrock, which I hope will be more of what I hoped to get out of Pathfinder.  I just don't think the long campaign thing is for me with this particular game.  I think this game may be too reliant on the appeal of slowly leveling up, and the game guts underneath aren't really interesting and varied enough to sustain the game long-term.

UPDATE June 2016
The app has revived this game for me.  I love it in the digital format.  No more endless card shuffling, no more finicky rules to figure out, and it feels much less repetitive becuase it moves muh faster.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Public service announcement for my board and card gaming brethren:

This is a card game. It is not a roleplaying game. While it can be confusing, because it has some of the surface trappings of popular conceptions of RPGs (namely a fantasy theme and persistant characters across sessions, although many RPGs don't have those at all), it is no more an RPG than Agricola is, even though you can pretend to be a farmer and tell a story about your family's economic fortunes.

Here is a simple rubric to help delineate: ask yourself, what takes precedence over what my character can do, the story or the rules? In an RPG, you can attempt anything you want, whether or not the rules specifically allow it. In a non-RPG, you can only do what the rules allow, even if it doesn't make sense. 

An example: in an RPG, two characters travel together to the village inn. This happens because of course two people can walk together somewhere. In the PACG, one person travels to the inn. The other person can't go yet because it's not his turn, even though in the story there is no reason why they can't travel together. The logic of the rules trumps the logic of the story. 

Anyway:

-----

Lightweight, breezy fun.  A game of resource and risk management, with a lot of clever ideas that reinforce the theme.  Persistent character decks that carry over between scenarios is great.

Scales very well across the player range.  More options to act/help when it's not your turn, or to peek ahead at the deck, would be good.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
(Comes with all expansion packs and character add-on deck)


The geekiest game I own, which also makes it the coolest.  I love card games.  I love hand management, trick taking, deckbuilding, and the uncertainty that comes with playing the odds.  I also really love getting new cards and abilities that amp you up as you play more games.  Pathfinder has all of this.  The overall game experience is extremely fun and rewarding - this game will probably usurp Dominion's four year reign as my favorite card game.  There's tons of replayability here, especially when it comes to deck building and customization.  I look forward to really wearing this game out.  It's awesome!

We finished playing all the scenarios in the base set and this game is more awesome than I originally thought - the emotional arcs that come with the dice rolls and card flips are really exhilirating, and the locations' abilities and deck compositions bring out the theme's juicy flavor.

Really fun game.  I'm always get a good laugh when I play it.  A tiger riding halfling with a flame enchanted sling squaring off against a hill giant down by the river is my idea of a good time.  This game is trying real hard to become my favorite and I'm having a hard time not letting it.

I stand by my rating of the base game, but the expansions really fail to take this game anywhere.  They're really just more of the same, and it can get kind of boring.  The dice rolls get really ridiculous too. If I had it to do all over again, I'd probably stop buying stuff at Hook Mountain, and I would have skipped on the character add-on deck.  

Another game will probably come along that stands on PACG's shoulders, and really knock it out of the park.  I wait impatiently.

RATING: 6
(Rating mainly based on solo play)

A light weight role playing game with kind of a deckbuilding element (you keep your deck and it changes over time). It's the perfect dungeon crawl game for me: Almost nonexistent story, fast play and most of the focus on upgrading your character. There's also almost no tactical movement. Normally you simply turn over the top card of the location you're at and deal with what comes up. It's kind of like Munchkin in that regard, but that's almost an insult.

However, the co-op element is not the strongest. Sure, you can work together, but if you have characters that can take care of themselves, you can go explore on your own - which I think is a good thing. The co-op element is probably most apparent when it comes to trading loot.

Negative points are that it almost takes too long to set up for what it is. There's a lot of searching for cards, distributing cards and shuffling cards. Your hands are busier setting up than actually playing the game because often times it's just flip over a card, roll a die and end your turn.

RATING: 5
First of all, I can’t help but compare the game to LOTR:TCG as I’m already committed to that one and wasn’t sure if I had the space in my gaming life to accommodate another coop LCG. I found I did because this was ostensibly less complicated (i.e., rules checking) than LOTR:TCG and for the way I could connect to a character who would progress through each scenario instead of just playing the blue deck, red/green deck, etc. I definitely have the geek “level up” gene and enjoy that kind of experience.

This process is nowhere near as diverse or interesting as LOTR:TCG manages. We like the way we interact in LOTR:TCG much more. Finally, I was put off by the way the next big box expansion is not compatible with characters from the Runelords base set and will require purchase.

RATING: 8
While the core mechanic of 'flip a card - make a skill check' may seem uninspiring at first glance, it turns out to be a very solid and flexible base mechanic to build a game around.  Each character has their own set of skills and their own strengths and weaknesses, and each challenge has it's own unique mechanics that are both thematic and serve to bring variety to the core mechanic.  Having multiple adventures in an adventure path, multiple scenarios in an adventure, and multiple locations in each scenario makes the game world feel appropriately expansive and, more importantly, expandable.  Each location has it's own small deck of challenges that must be overcome, and the villian and his henchmen are chased from from location to location in each scenario.  It all contributes greatly to capturing the feel of a much larger RPG adventure in a manageable amount of time.  A lot of thought and effort has gone into character progression, and it will take a lot of adventuring to 'max-out' a character.  Fortunately, the adventure path will ultimately be quite massive, and I have no doubt that completing it will bring a true sense of accompolishment.  Highly recommended. 

After a lot of play, I'm raising my rating by half a point.  The more I play it, the more I like it.  This game is right in my wheelhouse, and while not perfect, it's pretty damn close.  I find it more engaging than even LotR LCG or Star Wars LCG, both of which I like.

I own the full adventure path and the character add on deck. I've played 4 full play throughs. Really enjoyed each one. Haven't sleeved the cards and they are holding up just fine.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This game has really grabbed me. I've owned it about a month and have played through all available scenarios solo with a three-character party. So far I have played once with friends, and we'll be playing together again soon I'm sure. Although this is a shallow game in terms of strategy, there is a bit more to it than is at first apparent. For example, the decision to fix the built-in "timer" at 30 character turns regardless of the number of characters has a very interesting interaction with the discard-vs.-recharge card play mechanic. (Some cards must be discarded when they are played, some others must be recharged by adding them face-down to the bottom of the character's draw deck. Generally recharging is seen as being greatly preferable to discarding, and the card and character class balance take that into account.) Since a session with six characters likely will give only four or five turns to each character many will never get through their entire deck in order to take advantage of recharges. Why not discard instead? And of course with fewer characters recharging becomes very important. I anticipate finding more strategic subtleties as we play some more.

Component-wise, the box insert is wonderful although if you sleeve your cards (and given how much dang shuffling this game requires, why wouldn't you sleeve?) you'll run out of room quickly. The cards themselves are only okay:  good artwork but spartan design, below average card stock, some color variations between sets, some come wrapped so tightly that they remain bowed until sleeved. The rules are pretty well written but the publisher has had to post to their website numerous errata and clarifications. Let's hope that that type of thing improves with each release.

This is no Mage Knight, and yet I have more hours spent playing this solitaire than I have with Mage Knight. Sometimes a game-as-diversion while you listen to music and unwind from a hard day at work is just the thing you need.

RATING: 7.1
Gyakorlatilag egy kártyás szerepjáték. Annyira nem hasonlít a Thunderstone-ra, mint azt az ember elsőre gondolná. Egyrészt kooperatív, másrészt nagyon-nagyon kocka és egyéb szerencsevezérelt. Szóval inkább egy kártyás Descent. 
Tetszik benne, hogy lehet egy-egy gyors kalandot is nyomni, de hosszútávú karriereket is lehet játszani. Mindeközben fejlődnek a karakterek, tudnak egymással csereberélni stb. Ötletesen egyszerű a harc és az életerő kezelése. A húzópaklid az életerőd is egyben, ha elfogy meghaltál. Természetesen tudják fogyasztani a szörnyek, de fogy a varázslatok tárgyak használatától is, hisz folyamatosan fáradsz az utad során. Szellemes még a recharge azaz, hogy bizonyos lapokat bizonyos esetekben kijátszás után visszatehetsz a húzópaklid aljára, azaz nem fáradsz/sebződsz a használatuktól, ráadásul újra ki is játszhatod majd őket később. Tipikusan ilyenek a varázslatok, amiket megfelelő intelligencia check után vissza lehet pörgetni. 
Nagyon hangulatos még a scenariok összerakása is a helyszínekkel, random cuccokkal.

Node azért volt olyan is, ami nem annyira tetszik. Pl. pont a scenairoknál. Mivel teljesen randomok a kártyák a helyszíneken ezért elég faramuci dolgok tudnak kijönni. Pl. hegyi óriás bujkál a vásár forgatagában. A szerencse szerepe szinte kezelhetetlenül nagy, főleg a kártyasorrendet illetően. Egyszerűen képtelenség megcsinálni egy-egy forgatókönyvet, ha minden főgonosz a paklija aljára kerül. A doboz elsőre nagyon okosan beosztottnak tűnt. Szokás szerint ez addig volt így, amíg nem akartam kártyavédőzni, mert úgy már szinte az alap kártyák se férnek el az insertben, miközben a doboz fele elmegy az üres kiegdobozok majdani tárolására fenntartott helynek. Insane.

Összességében egy jó kis szerepjáték adaptáció kártyára. Ha nem zavar, hogy szinte csak a szerencsén múlik a party sorsa, és bele tudod élni magad a történetbe, akkor nagyon jó kis játék tud lenni. Nekem ez azért nem megy 100%-osan.

-> 6.8

----
Update: Többen azért lényegesen nagyobb a kombózási lehetőség. Szinte minden checket tudunk teljesíteni, csak kérdés, hogy mire mennyit érdemes áldozni. Van mit megbeszélni, kitalálni mindenkinek akár a másik körében is, szóval gyakorlatilag nincs holtidő. Igaz, így meg a sztoriba lehet kevésbé elmerülni, mert nincs nagyon idő helyszínkártyákat olvasgatni.

RATING: 8
It's an RPG simulator attempt. It fell flat on my first play, which admittedly, was a bit rushed. But it was basically, go to a location, flip a card, decide if it was worth augmenting a roll to acquire, and roll the required die. To its credit, the game did move, but it was not tense at all. When we were done, we looked at each other and shrugged, saying, "I guess we lost." There was little exciting to me about a game where winning meant finding the right card that was randomly shuffled into a number of decks.

However, after playing the three scenarios of the first campaign out of the box: holy wow. Everything awesome about this game is in: 
A - understanding how to work the rules of the game 

B - leveling your character and adjusting him between scenarios. Then you get completely excited to watch him become better and stronger for the next game. This design is genius in how the character development works.

Long story short: don't judge this game on a single play. Judge it on a series of plays, because where it shines strongest is the character build.

RATING: 8
I was surprised how much I liked this. I went in a little nervous that it would simply feel like a game where you roll dice forever and do skill checks ad infinitum. Funny enough, that is sort of what it is but beyond that there is a sense of visiting different locations, looking for various treasures, friends, and abilities while fighting monsters, henchmen, and villains.  There is variety in how everything plays out and resolves so it keeps you entertained. The graphics are quite good, but are just on the edge of not being great.  There is little ambiguity in the card text but enough holes in the rulebook that things were a bit frustrating during our first game. I am afraid that there's not a lot of room for growth in concept beyond the first few games; and this only scares me because of how many expansions there are. I hope the game can create a sense of growth because I could see myself tiring of it if this was all it had to offer in the end. But for now, there's something very satisfying about playing a scenario out and I'm not sure what more could be done to give players the feeling of an RPG in a card game. Rating may go down some day, but for now it's a high rating.

RATING: 7
Pathfinder ACG is a condensed version of the RPG. It excels at capturing the health, items and abilities through a deck builder all within a solo / coop experience. The location decks generally feel unique and thematic. 

The constant dice rolling against checks can get a bit monotonous. Also, the difficulty on this version is a bit on the easy side. Many of the challenges and monsters you can just beat your way through.

Last gripe is that it feels like the players are just playing individual solo games and can't (really) interact much on other players' turns.

It's a great attempt at RPG / Card Game hybrid and look forward to playing many of the different versions.

RATING: 6
I like it, but don't love it.  I [had] a complete game with every adventure and the character add-on (and even some promo cards).

It's pretty easy, really, and not fun to loose (unlike some better co-operative games.  As a result it really suffers from the alpha gamer problem because there is usually a correct choice.

Especially when it takes so long to set up.  

Don't get me wrong, it's good.  But it's a really big game of solitaire at the end of the day.  Also, the inability to predict what types of cards will emerge for matching with character abilities is a big game design problem, ESPECIALLY for a cooperative game.  Once again, I play alone with only two characters.

At first, I really liked this game with my SO.  If does tell an interesting story, and I could see it being the perfect game for someone.  It's just not enough game for me (despite coming in a rather large box)

Traded away

RATING: 7
I really do not know how I feel about this game.  It could go way up, or way down.  I have the whole first cycle adventure packs and feel no compulsion to own more.

I love the campaign system, leveling and item deck construction.  I anticipate seeing huge numbers of copy cats from here on in.  That said... the game itself is a straightforward flip up a card and encounter system, with a skill check generally involved.  I'm ok with that, but this first cycle has had way too many base scenario "hunt the henchman" scenarios.  It's a huge missed opportunity, I think you could do something special with this system with better scenarios.

That said, this game is never going to provide brain busting decisions, nor is it intended too.  The question is if it has just enough decisions to stay interesting---it's a game that you can idly play while talking with someone and that is not necessarily a bad thing.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Hi, my name is THEME and I do not appear in this game in any tangible, relateable way. Thanks for your concern, but I'm not here. Please look elsewhere.
Yes, it's true. It looks like THEME is here. It looks that way on the box. The PATHFINDER brand name alone represents potential theme, and the basic substance of that theme is, in fact, here. But after you open the lid, set up the game and take your first action, the theme lies on it's side, heaves it's last breath and promptly dies like a Christmas puppy wrapped in a gift box with no air holes.
"Dear God! That's just horrible!" you're saying.
I know! How do you think I feel?
How can they get so close to creating a world class dungeon crawl and yet so terribly miss the mark?

Other than thematic puppy-cide, the game actually works.
And that may be the reason for all the hype. 
Its mechanics flow in a well designed card game that shows you how well a card game...can...be...designed.
But that's all it does.
Although, it does it very well. 
Characters that level up and gain new abilities each time you play? WORKS.
New equipment, spells, and monsters to face in each new upgrade pack? WORKS.
Combat options and choices that could leave your character and all you worked for dead? Yep. WORKS.
 
I like that it works. It works so well, that my son and I played this game over and over. I've bought expansions for it. I bought additional characters. Why? 
Because.
I'm a collector? I like expansions? I have disposable income?
Okay, it's none of your business why.
Just- because, that's why.
Leave me alone.
 
I keep thinking I'll introduce this game to some of my other board game friends, but I never do.
I love what the designers set out to do with this game, and I hate that it ultimately DOESN'T WORK.
There are rave reviews out there, but this game isn't what it pretends to be. It's an effective, well designed card game with a sliver of theme just like Dominion, but lacking that game's depth, replayability, and strategy.
Maybe some future expansions will fix the theme issue, but by that time, you could have learned to played Descent, or any other dungeon crawler, or even the real Pathfinder game. Of course, then you'd be a nerd, and all wrapped up in the role-playing culture, standing around Comic-Con in your underwear calling it cos-play.
And we can't have that now, can we?
It's weird. I love it, but I can't recommend it.
Sorry, guys.
